        #region WriteLineInColor Methods
        public void WriteLineInColor (
            ConsoleColor pclrForeColor ,
            ConsoleColor pclrBackColor ,
            bool value )
        {
            this.ChangeColors ( pclrForeColor , pclrBackColor );
            Console.Write ( value );
            this.RestoreOrigColors ( );
        }   // public void WriteLineInColor (1 of 18)

        /// <summary>
        /// Write the string representation of a bool (Boolean) variable.
        /// </summary>
        /// <param name="pclrForeColor">
        /// Specify the ConsoleColor to use for the foreground (text).
        /// </param>
        /// <param name="pclrBackColor">
        /// Specify the ConsoleColor to use for the background.
        /// </param>
        /// <param name="value">
        /// Specify the Boolean value to display.
        /// </param>
        public void WriteMessageInColor (
            ConsoleColor pclrForeColor ,
            ConsoleColor pclrBackColor ,
            bool value )
        {
            this.ChangeColors ( pclrForeColor , pclrBackColor );
            Console.Write ( value );
            this.RestoreOrigColors ( );
        }   // public void WriteMessageInColor (1 of 18)

        /// <summary>
        /// Write a formatted message that includes the string representation of

        /// </summary>
        /// <param name="pclrForeColor">

        /// </param>
        /// <param name="pclrBackColor">
        /// Specify the ConsoleColor to use for the background.
        /// </param>
        /// <param name="format">
        /// Use this string as the message template, which may include at most
        /// one substitution token.
        /// </param>
        /// <param name="arg0">
        /// Replace the substition token with the string representation of this
        /// generic object.
        /// </param>
        public void WriteMessageInColor (
            ConsoleColor pclrForeColor ,
            ConsoleColor pclrBackColor ,
            string format ,
            object arg0 )

            this.ChangeColors ( pclrForeColor , pclrBackColor );

        /// <summary>
        /// Write a formatted message that includes the string representation of
        /// an generic object variable.
        /// </summary>
        /// <param name="pclrForeColor">
        /// Specify the ConsoleColor to use for the foreground (text).
        /// </param>
        /// <param name="pclrBackColor">
        /// Specify the ConsoleColor to use for the background.
        /// </param>
        /// <param name="format">
        /// Use this string as the message template, which may contains
        /// substitution tokens for each object in an array of generic Object
        /// variables.
        /// </param>
        /// <param name="arg">
        /// Substitute elements from this array of generic Object variables into
        /// the format string, replacing tokens with the element whose subscript
        /// is the number within its brackets.
        /// </param>
        public void WriteMessageInColor (
            ConsoleColor pclrForeColor ,
            ConsoleColor pclrBackColor ,
            string format ,
            params object [ ] arg )
        {
            this.ChangeColors ( pclrForeColor , pclrBackColor );
            Console.Write ( format , arg );
            this.RestoreOrigColors ( );
        }   // public void WriteMessageInColor (14 of 18)


        /// <summary>
        /// Write a formatted message that includes a range of characters taken
        /// from an array of Unicode characters.
        /// </summary>
        /// <param name="pclrForeColor">
        /// Specify the ConsoleColor to use for the foreground (text).
        /// </param>
        /// <param name="pclrBackColor">
        /// Specify the ConsoleColor to use for the background.
        /// </param>
        /// <param name="format">
        /// Use this string as the message template, which may contains
        /// substitution tokens for count number of characters.
        /// </param>
        /// <param name="buffer">
        /// Extract characters from this array of Unicode characters.
        /// </param>
        /// <param name="index">
        /// Subscript of character to substitute for token {0} in format.
        /// </param>
        /// <param name="count">
        /// Number of characters from buffer to substitute into string, which
        /// must contain at least count - 1 substitution tokens.
        /// </param>
        public void WriteMessageInColor (
            ConsoleColor pclrForeColor ,
            ConsoleColor pclrBackColor ,
            string format ,
            char [ ] buffer ,
            int index ,
            int count )
        {
            this.ChangeColors ( pclrForeColor , pclrBackColor );
            Console.Write ( buffer , index , count );
            this.RestoreOrigColors ( );
        }   // public void WriteMessageInColor (15 of 18)


        /// <summary>

        /// </summary>

        /// </param>
        /// <param name="format">
        /// Use this string as the message template, which may contain up to two
        /// substition tokens, {0} and {1}.
        /// </param>

        /// The default string representation of this generic Object variable is
        /// substituted into format for token {0}.

Replace "MessageColors" with "MessageInColor" in worksheet Properties.Resources
of Technical_Documentation_Worksheets.XLSX.

MessageBox, its text is opaque to the Windows clipboard. Hence, it must actually
belong to another window class.

MessageInColor_Source_Code

================================================================================
=RIGHT(A1,LEN(A1)-FIND("~",SUBSTITUTE(A1,"\","~",LEN(A1)-LEN(SUBSTITUTE(A1,"\","")))))
=RIGHT(A1,LEN(A1)-FIND("~",SUBSTITUTE(A1," ","~",LEN(A1)-LEN(SUBSTITUTE(A1," ","")))))
=RIGHT(B2,LEN(B2)-FIND("~",SUBSTITUTE(B2," ","~",LEN(B2)-LEN(SUBSTITUTE(B2," ","")))))
=if(C2,RIGHT(B2,LEN(B2)-FIND("~",SUBSTITUTE(B2," ","~",LEN(B2)-LEN(SUBSTITUTE(B2," ",""))))),"")

Reference:	"Find the last occurrence of a character in a string"
			http://www.excelforum.com/excel-general/601021-find-the-last-occurrence-of-a-character-in-a-string.html

This isn't exactly what I would call the "last occurrance," but it's a start in
that direction.
================================================================================

MessageInColor


=if(e1971=f1971,RIGHT(B2,LEN(B2)-FIND("~",SUBSTITUTE(B2," ","~",LEN(B2)-LEN(SUBSTITUTE(B2," ",""))))),"")

left(B1971,e1971-2)
=if(c1971,if(e1971=f1971,RIGHT(left(B1971,e1971-2),LEN(left(B1971,e1971-2))-FIND("~",SUBSTITUTE(left(B1971,e1971-2)," ","~",LEN(left(B1971,e1971-2))-LEN(SUBSTITUTE(left(B1971,e1971-2)," ",""))))),d1971,"")

02/01/2014 00:53:38 - How to use column labels to make VLookup self adjusting.
================================================================================

See the Match function in all but the first two rows of column D in worksheet
ChangeColors Methods of Excel workbook Technical_Documentation_Worksheets.XLSX.

Reference:	"Dynamic searching using VLOOKUP, MATCH and INDEX"
			http://office.microsoft.com/en-us/excel-help/dynamic-searching-using-vlookup-match-and-index-HA001154902.aspx
================================================================================
"Excel Indirect function," at http://www.meadinkent.co.uk/xl-indirect.htm may be
what I need to make those formulas that treat labels as range names.
